In [25]:
print(completeness_score(t,clusterAssignment))

0.612634628644
In [26]:
print(homogeneity_score(t,clusterAssignment))

0.610934710766
From the values above, we see there is some disagreement between our assignment and the ones assigned. If all the data points that are members of a given class are elements of the same cluster, the completeness score would be one. If all the clusters contained data points that are member of a single class, the homogeneity would be one.¶

B) Complete the definition for the function "test". This function iterates over all users and for each performs cross-validation on items (by calling the provided "cross_validate_user" function), and returns the error information necessary to compute Mean Absolute Error (MAE). Use this function to perform 5-fold cross-validation (i.e., 20% test-ratio) comparing MAE results using standard item-based collaborative filtering (based on the rating prediction function "standEst") with results using the SVD-based version of the rating item-based CF¶

In [65]:
def test(dataMat, test_ratio, estMethod):
    total_error=0.0
    total_count=0
    for user in range(dataMat.shape[0]):
        error, count = cross_validate_user(dataMat, user, .2, standEst)
        total_error = total_error + error
        total_count = total_count + count
    MAE = total_error/total_count
    print ('Mean Absoloute Error for ',estMethod,' : ', MAE)
    return MAE

C) Write a new function "print_most_similar_jokes" which takes the joke ratings data, a query joke id, a parameter k for the number of nearest neighbors, and a similarity metric function, and prints the text of the query joke as well as the texts of the top k most similar jokes based on user ratings.¶

In [67]:
def pearsSim(inA,inB):
    if len(inA) < 3 : return 1.0
    return 0.5 + 0.5 * corrcoef(inA, inB, rowvar = 0)[0][1]
